<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_215b0e56-ec3d-4e67-832c-dd6051c0e79e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/123290012-eugenia-tur"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1603268184i/123290012._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/123290012-eugenia-tur">Eugenia Tur</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I will decompose a little bit the answer. Kids all ages SHOULD read this book and adults all ages SHOULD HAVE READ this book. <br/><br/>It is quite poetical and<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I will decompose a little bit the answer. Kids all ages SHOULD read this book and adults all ages SHOULD HAVE READ this book. <br /><br />It is quite poetical and melodic, so if you read it to them, you should practice getting the best out of it. Also, if you can trigger a conversation afterward involving the bigger kids and adults, you can really get all the juice out of it. <br /><br />You should see all Dr. Seuss books as a chance to educate people of all ages. He does write some funny stories, but he also teaches lessons and gives the tools to improve our and our children’s mindset. <br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <a title="Michael Finocchiaro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48483884-michael-finocchiaro"><img alt="Michael Finocchiaro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576692048p2/48483884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1781509436?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Finocchiaro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Finocchiaro" href="/user/show/48483884-michael-finocchiaro">Michael Finocchiaro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=kids">kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=american-20th-c">american-20th-c</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1781509436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12799105382548705132">Now who would have thought that Seuss back in the 60’s would have already been concerned about the destruction of the environment – so much so that he wrote this incredible and addictive story (asked for by my son two to three times a week). My kid is always asking me about the Once-ler “Why can’t we see his body? Why did he make the Barba-loots go away? Why did he cut down the Truffula tree? What is a Thneed?” The lessons are so simple and yet so subtle here – and it is great on so many differe</span>
  <span id="freeText12799105382548705132" style="display:none">Now who would have thought that Seuss back in the 60’s would have already been concerned about the destruction of the environment – so much so that he wrote this incredible and addictive story (asked for by my son two to three times a week). My kid is always asking me about the Once-ler “Why can’t we see his body? Why did he make the Barba-loots go away? Why did he cut down the Truffula tree? What is a Thneed?” The lessons are so simple and yet so subtle here – and it is great on so many different levels. The Thneed question makes me almost blush because I have so many thneeds (iPhone, iPad, Mac, Cinema Display, PS3, etc). Who else would have thought of such a perfect word like thneeds. Or sluppity slupp and gloopity gloop. Tonight my son wanted me to show him a Whisper-ma-phone and to hear a snargley voice. What can I say? It is a story that I can STRONGLY recommend to anyone reading this blog and especially to the kids of my readers. I just hope that the UNLESS will be applicable to the generation after ours with our Valdeses and Fukushimas…of course are not directly the fault of our generation but then our generation hasn’t really made headway in preventing these disasters either.<br />I just hope that I don’t glow in the dark as I walk through the grickle grass eating humming fish sushi.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12799105382548705132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10133405587075980288" style="display:none">January 2015<br /><br />A one-paragraph review of a children's book I didn't like has generated more trolls and their inevitable sock puppet alteregos than any other of my reviews, I've lost count of the number of them. But what is there about this review or about the book that generates this kind of over-the-top reaction from obviously mentally-unstable individuals? <br />_____<br /><br />Maybe I'm just not a Dr. Seuss person but I hated this book. Boring story, stupid words that didn't entertain and even though it was meant for a child rather than me, my son hardly ever looked at it growing up, so its sits on the shelf still quite pristine. <br /><br />Funny thing is that this is only a comment on a kiddies' book - yet it has engendered so much nastiness from several people all of whom appear to be alteregos of Michael. He has made it his business to take people (not me alone) to task for not enjoying this book even to the extent of making personal remarks. He himself enjoys it so much he's made a society (IRL not virtually) to promote its aims as thought it were a kind of bible. Luckily the other reviewers are more rational and measured in their response and don't feel the need to make rude personal remarks. Each to his own. This isn't for me.<br /><br />May 2010<br /><br />I was just looking through my reviews and noticed that Corky and two other characters (the same person?) have deleted their reviews and their IDs.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20445736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10676072982937594846">You can have your <i> Silent Spring</i> and <i>Inconvenient Truth</i>. The Lorax and his lesson of unless is, to me, the most moving piece of environmental literature ever. It shows that a) good children's literature doesn't have to be simplistic or happy to be effective and b) that you certainly need not be a member of a political group to appreciate the message that our drive to industrialize must not happen at the expense of our planet.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15856273347201266533">The Lorax, Dr. Seuss<br/>The Lorax is a children's book written by Dr. Seuss and first published in 1971. It chronicles the plight of the environment and the Lorax is the titular character, who "speaks for the trees" and confronts the Once-ler, who causes environmental destruction. As in most Dr. Seuss books, the creatures mentioned are typically unique to the story. A young unnamed boy living in a polluted area visits a strange isolated man called the Once-ler on the Street of the Lifted Lorax. The </span>
  <span id="freeText15856273347201266533" style="display:none">The Lorax, Dr. Seuss<br />The Lorax is a children's book written by Dr. Seuss and first published in 1971. It chronicles the plight of the environment and the Lorax is the titular character, who "speaks for the trees" and confronts the Once-ler, who causes environmental destruction. As in most Dr. Seuss books, the creatures mentioned are typically unique to the story. A young unnamed boy living in a polluted area visits a strange isolated man called the Once-ler on the Street of the Lifted Lorax. The boy pays the Once-ler fifteen cents, a nail, and the shell of a great-great-great grandfather snail to hear the legend of how the Lorax was lifted and taken away. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین نگرش: روز بیست و پنجم ماه سپتامبر سال 2008 میلادی<br />عنوان: لوراکس؛ زیوس (سوس، سئوس)؛ مترجم: رضی هیرمندی؛ تهران: افق، کتابهای فندق، 1386؛ در 48 ص؛ مصور؛ شابک: 9789643694197؛ گروه سنی: ب، ج؛ چاپ دوم: تهران: نشر افق، کتابهای فندق‏‫، 1392؛ در 70 ص، شابک: 9789643699215؛ موضوع: داستانهای طنز (خنده دار) برای کودکان - از نویسندگان ایالات متحده امریکا - سده 20 م<br />عنوان: لوراکس؛ نویسنده: سئوس؛ مترجم: راحله مرادی؛ تهران: آشنایی‏‫، 1389؛ در 56 ص؛ مصور، رنگی، شابک: 9789647063647؛ ‬چاپ دوم 1394؛ چاپ سوم 1396؛<br /><br />رخدادهای زیست محیطی را برای کودکان بازگو میکندد، درباره درخت مهربانی به نام «لوراکس» است، که نسلش توسط بازرگانی سودجو به خطر میافتد، اما داستان را پسرکی بنام «تد» میچرخاند، که برای بدست آوردن دختر آرزوهایش باید به خواسته ی او تن دهد تا ....؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8910586904485615521">I'm not a real big fan of Dr. Suess. I've never enjoyed the made up language that seems to be in every book he writes. However, I've always made an exception for the Lorax. Although there is plenty of made up language in this book too, it doesn't take me out of the story. And I like the story and the overall message of the book. It would definitely be a good book for Earth Day .</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_87798963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87798963" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87798963?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=banned-books">banned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=children-s-book">children-s-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=picture-book">picture-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=environmentalism">environmentalism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=animal-books">animal-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87798963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4273542324067568738">“The Lorax” is one of Dr. Seuss’ most memorable books as it is about the importance of taking care of all of the trees in the world. “The Lorax” may have some controversial issues, but it is still a great book for both children and adults to treasure for many years.<br/><br/>Dr. Seuss’ story about how chopping down too many trees can destroy the Earth’s environment is truly powerful and moving as it realistically portrays what can happen to the environment when trees are cut down through Dr. Seuss’ childi</span>
  <span id="freeText4273542324067568738" style="display:none">“The Lorax” is one of Dr. Seuss’ most memorable books as it is about the importance of taking care of all of the trees in the world. “The Lorax” may have some controversial issues, but it is still a great book for both children and adults to treasure for many years.<br /><br />Dr. Seuss’ story about how chopping down too many trees can destroy the Earth’s environment is truly powerful and moving as it realistically portrays what can happen to the environment when trees are cut down through Dr. Seuss’ childish world. Dr. Seuss’ illustrations as always are extremely creative and inventive especially when we are first introduced to the land of the Truffula trees, the land is colourful and peaceful looking, but when the once-ler starts cutting down all the Truffula trees, the land looks dark and bleak, representing the pollution that is caused from cutting down the trees.<br /><br />Parents should know that even though I personally do not see anything wrong with this book, this book was considered extremely controversial due to the fact that many people believed that the book was trying to promote the idea that industrialization is a bad thing. Personally, I think that this book was just trying to discuss about the issues of environmentalism and that cutting down too many trees can cause pollution on the earth.<br /><br />“The Lorax” is one of the greatest books about the issues of environmentalism that kids will understand perfectly and will definitely be evolved into one of the greatest cult classics to ever come to the world of children’s books. I would recommend this book to children ages five and up due to the controversial material about whether or not industrialization is a good or bad thing for the world that small children might not understand. <br /><br /><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/08/the-lorax-by-dr-seuss.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4273542324067568738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17531084699427608046"><b>5 A wonderful story with a POWERFUL message! ★'s</b> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“I am the Lorax. I speak for the trees. I speak for the trees for the trees have no tongues.”</i>
</b> <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542006262i/26581913._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Oh. My. Goodness! *in a singsong voice* I love, I love, I loovvve, <i>The Lorax</i> :) Seriously though this book right here is so so special! I know I say this like all the time but whatever... this is another one of my FAVORITE <i>Dr. Seuss</i> books. I mean HELLO it's <i>Dr. Seuss</i> for crying out loud, of course, it's amazing. I love all of his crazy, weird, cute, u</span>
  <span id="freeText17531084699427608046" style="display:none"><b>5 A wonderful story with a POWERFUL message! ★'s</b> <br><br><b>
  <i>“I am the Lorax. I speak for the trees. I speak for the trees for the trees have no tongues.”</i>
</b> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542006262i/26581913._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Oh. My. Goodness! *in a singsong voice* I love, I love, I loovvve, <i>The Lorax</i> :) Seriously though this book right here is so so special! I know I say this like all the time but whatever... this is another one of my FAVORITE <i>Dr. Seuss</i> books. I mean HELLO it's <i>Dr. Seuss</i> for crying out loud, of course, it's amazing. I love all of his crazy, weird, cute, unique and special characters he's able to bring to life. They all are truly something else. In all honesty though <i>The Lorax</i> has got to be <i>Dr. Seuss</i>'s most serious of all his books, he really tones down all the silliness that's in his other books and really tries to drive his point across. Point being we need care about our environment and that we have got to treat it right! To help drive this point the illustrations start out so bleak and lifeless, in all shades of greys and then once the story gets going the colors turn so vivid and bright and beautiful, just to fade back into grey as the trees start getting cut down :( The illustrations are incredible! If your looking to read something goofy this isn't it but if you're interested in reading something with a powerful message... Look no further for you have found it. <br><br><b>
  <i>“It's not about what it is, it's about what it can become.” <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542006262i/26581914.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>*The movie was brilliant!! I have seen it so many times it's not even funny and now thanks to writing this review I must... I MUST. Watch it again tonight! haha*</b> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542006534ra/26581917.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542006262ra/26581911.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542006262ra/26581912.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_208852025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208852025" />
    <a title="Robert Bickers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6099869-robert-bickers"><img alt="Robert Bickers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388632296p2/6099869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208852025?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert Bickers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert Bickers" href="/user/show/6099869-robert-bickers">Robert Bickers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208852025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17841326140593732314">Ok, so it's a heavy-handed enviromental terror-tale. It's also the Seuss book that stuck with me the longest. Of all the books I read as a little kid, it's the one that I still remember making me feel something.<br/><br/>I'm a conservationist-not an environmentalist by any stretch. <i>The Lorax</i> didn't teach me to hate industry or chew on organically-sustainable bark. It taught me to care about nature. To this day, decades after I read and re-read it, the drawing of the barren wasteland still gets to me.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3079874431" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5349063844851353610">I didn't think I'd read this one, but as I turned the pages, the memories started to come back to me. It was the Brown Bar-ba-loots that stuck in my head for some reason...<br/><br/>In any case, this is a rather modern-sounding tale about conservation. It's just as appropriate for today's audiences as it would have been when it was first published. <i>The Lorax</i> contains a story within a story told by a mysterious character called the Once-ler, who tells of a time when Truffula Trees grew plentiful, supplying</span>
  <span id="freeText5349063844851353610" style="display:none">I didn't think I'd read this one, but as I turned the pages, the memories started to come back to me. It was the Brown Bar-ba-loots that stuck in my head for some reason...<br><br>In any case, this is a rather modern-sounding tale about conservation. It's just as appropriate for today's audiences as it would have been when it was first published. <i>The Lorax</i> contains a story within a story told by a mysterious character called the Once-ler, who tells of a time when Truffula Trees grew plentiful, supplying the Brown Bar-ba-loots with shade and food. But the Once-ler figures out that he can knit with the tufts of the Truffula Trees, and this spells the end of the natural paradise. A creature called the Lorax, who speaks for the trees, warns the Once-ler that he's doing harm... but the Once-ler cares only about money.<br><br>I found the writing in this a bit iffy, and the meter isn't as strong as it is in some of Dr. Seuss's other books. Still, the message is important enough that I'm willing to overlook some of these issues.<br><br>The story ends with a bit of hope, but the depiction of what happens from unchecked industry and greed is bleak. It's definitely a timely tale, and one that is perfectly appropriate--necessary, even--for today's kids.<br><br><b>Quotable moment:</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576006753i/28591472._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_12104716" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/12104716" />
    <a title="Skylar Burris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/710201-skylar-burris"><img alt="Skylar Burris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449959508p2/710201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12104716?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skylar Burris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skylar Burris" href="/user/show/710201-skylar-burris">Skylar Burris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/710201-skylar-burris?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12104716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13637971555367246570">This gets five stars for being beautifully written, and one for being heavy handed, which averages out to four for me. I'm a conservationist, but there is no nuance in The Lorax's presentation of environmentalism: the book simply demonizes business. <br/><br/>The Once-ler is an extreme negative caricature of the capitalist: what he offers society as an entrepreneur is not valuable in any way, he has no regard for anything but his own profit, and he proceeds with reckless abandon. Of course, in a world tha</span>
  <span id="freeText13637971555367246570" style="display:none">This gets five stars for being beautifully written, and one for being heavy handed, which averages out to four for me. I'm a conservationist, but there is no nuance in The Lorax's presentation of environmentalism: the book simply demonizes business. <br /><br />The Once-ler is an extreme negative caricature of the capitalist: what he offers society as an entrepreneur is not valuable in any way, he has no regard for anything but his own profit, and he proceeds with reckless abandon. Of course, in a world that is not an emotionally manipulative moral fable, the Once-ler would have planted many more Truffula trees LONG before they became extinct, because when a resource is profitable and replenishable, any capitalist with even half a brain replenishes it. On the other hand, I suppose the Lorax could be said also to be an extreme negative caricature of the environmentalist: he pops on the scene sporadically to scold with righteous indignation, offers no compromise, accomplishes nothing, leaves the costs of realizing his cause to others, and literally flies by the seat of his pants. (And yet I've never heard an environmentalist complain about the Lorax's lack of complexity.)<br /><br />Nevertheless, despite its caricatures and lack of nuance, I cannot deny the overall quality and effect of the story. The mood setting is phenomenal, and I'm always amazed that the Dr. Seuss books, no matter how long, hold my preschooler's attention the entire time. Other books half that long would not do so. I don't remember particularly caring about this one when I read it as a child. As an adult, however, from a purely literary perspective, it strikes me as being among his best. It's a superbly effective piece of propaganda, and, if I weren’t so concerned about balance, compromise, and critical thinking, I'd give it five stars. Perhaps, however, I shouldn't be so concerned: after all, isn't most children's literature painted in sweeping strokes of black and white? Children don't think with the critical faculties of adults, and what is my daughter really going to take away from this? (A) Capitalism is evil and I should never start my own business, or (B) I should plant a tree! I hope it will be only (B), and (B) is not a bad thing at all.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13637971555367246570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hákon Gunnarsson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hákon Gunnarsson" href="/user/show/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson">Hákon Gunnarsson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson?shelf=climate-crisis">climate-crisis</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3388480166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4209221589516313817">I think The Lorax is very topical children’s book even though it was first published in 1971. It seems to fit right into the dialog taking place about ecological matters today. If one would for example read this with the destruction of the Amazon in mind. Reading it really feels like it was written as an response to that, but of course it wasn’t. It kind of tells one how little has changed in 50 years.<br/><br/>We still need someone to talk for the trees, the animals, the birds, the fish, and for nature a</span>
  <span id="freeText4209221589516313817" style="display:none">I think The Lorax is very topical children’s book even though it was first published in 1971. It seems to fit right into the dialog taking place about ecological matters today. If one would for example read this with the destruction of the Amazon in mind. Reading it really feels like it was written as an response to that, but of course it wasn’t. It kind of tells one how little has changed in 50 years.<br /><br />We still need someone to talk for the trees, the animals, the birds, the fish, and for nature as a whole.<br /><br />There is one thing though, it’s not a terribly fun book. It doesn’t have a engaging plot. In fact, the plot is a bit depressing, but that is perhaps basically because the subject is depressing. How does one explain to children the destruction of nature as it is going on right now, without being a bit depressed? If you know, please let me know because I would really like to know. As it stands, I think I would say that this is a very good book to explain to children what is going on with our relationship with nature. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4209221589516313817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007173112" href="/book/show/235061.The_Lorax">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12723605-cruth?shelf=read-aloud">read-aloud</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer551355866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14088766590453707398"><i>Unless someone like you cares a whole awful lot,<br/>nothing is going to get better. It's not.</i><br/><br/>Author/Illustrator: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6953473.Dr_Seuss' title='Dr Seuss' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dr Seuss</a><br/>First published: 1971<br/><br/>The ankle-biter had seen the animated movie <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1482459/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lorax</a> with her cousins and was keen to read the book. I was wary because a) I understood the movie was substantially different to the book, and b) her reading ability (vocab and comprehension) IMO surpassed Dr Seuss. BUT she'd been "studying" Dr Seuss at school in relation to <i>poetry</i> so I picked up the book and mo</span>
  <span id="freeText14088766590453707398" style="display:none"><i>Unless someone like you cares a whole awful lot,<br />nothing is going to get better. It's not.</i><br /><br />Author/Illustrator: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6953473.Dr_Seuss" title="Dr Seuss" rel="nofollow noopener">Dr Seuss</a><br />First published: 1971<br /><br />The ankle-biter had seen the animated movie <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1482459/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lorax</a> with her cousins and was keen to read the book. I was wary because a) I understood the movie was substantially different to the book, and b) her reading ability (vocab and comprehension) IMO surpassed Dr Seuss. BUT she'd been "studying" Dr Seuss at school in relation to <i>poetry</i> so I picked up the book and movie for some family time.<br /><br />And found an unexpectedly enjoyable book with a lesson on conservation, deforestation and anti-consumerism. Typical of Dr Seuss the language has a beautiful rhythm, rhyme and humour which just screams "Read Aloud!".<br /><br />I'm putting my prejudices aside and pulling out the Dr Seuss to mix with the Dahl's. They are fun, and they encourage the listener to participate and enjoy *language*.<br /><br /><b>Extras</b><br />- Classroom discussion questions from <a href="http://www.seussville.com/Educators/lorax_classroom/educatorlorax_discuss.php" rel="nofollow noopener">Seussville .com</a>.<br />-There are various Lorax Apps available including <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/the-official-lorax-app/id474779698?mt=8" rel="nofollow noopener">the official one</a>, <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/au/app/the-lorax-dr.-seuss/id367260225?mt=8" rel="nofollow noopener">a storybook app</a> .<br /><br /><b>Phonics vs Whole Language</b><br />The school my daughters attend has always used a combination of phonics and whole language to teach reading. They were given "sight words" to learn - pattern match the word without thinking about the letters and sounds they make, as well as placing the word within the reading context to "guess" what it would be. And they were shown how to break a word into bite-size chunks to sound out the word.<br /><br />Dr Seuss (and in this context, "The Lorax") won't allow a reader to depend solely on one method. His original words ("Barbaloots", "Truffula") require a phonetic interpretation, but also the contextual understanding to make sense of them. And then there are his rhymes which defy a purely phonetic reading (eg trees and please, "Barbaloot suit"). It makes his books a greater challenge, and also a more interesting read, than many adults (including me) realise.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teaching_reading:_whole_language_and_phonics">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teaching...</a><br /> <br /><b>Age</b> (taking into account comprehension, concentration, language):<br />Read aloud - 5+<br />Read yourself - 7+ (typical Suess playing with words makes a once simple vocabulary challenging)<br /><br />(ISBN 9780007173112)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14088766590453707398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1545242833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14826348614067010283">Has nobody read this book? All these years and we are still chopping down trees, creating loads of pollution and happily killing off animals.<br/><br/>This has to be Dr. Seuss's most serious book, he tones down the silliness and tries to get across his warning. The illustrations are wonderful, the start is so bleak and drab, all shades of grey and once the story gets told the colours are so vivid they jump out of the page at you, only for you to watch the grey come back as the trees get cut down.<br/><br/>Wonderful</span>
  <span id="freeText14826348614067010283" style="display:none">Has nobody read this book? All these years and we are still chopping down trees, creating loads of pollution and happily killing off animals.<br /><br />This has to be Dr. Seuss's most serious book, he tones down the silliness and tries to get across his warning. The illustrations are wonderful, the start is so bleak and drab, all shades of grey and once the story gets told the colours are so vivid they jump out of the page at you, only for you to watch the grey come back as the trees get cut down.<br /><br />Wonderful story telling with a powerful message.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('C+ccMWeWZLURT1X7QK9w18ZTXytf7hvk4yZ+04mYHLk97zPQt8Rh9ynl8C983wCm7vyVQSt4p6HO2iFRvtjecg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Coa4+7rUJIq30GLLjCYOorbE6yBs2hIpKDCsFk9g2eI8jpcaaoYhyI96xx+wVn7TnmshShhMrmwFzPOUeCAbKQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/61105.Dr_Seuss">About Dr. Seuss</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/61105.Dr_Seuss"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1193930952p3/61105.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/61105.Dr_Seuss">Dr. Seuss
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15462928492295742856">Theodor Seuss Geisel was born 2 March 1904 in Springfield, MA. He graduated Dartmouth College in 1925, and proceeded on to Oxford University with the intent of acquiring a doctorate in literature. At Oxford he met Helen Palmer, who he wed in 1927. He returned from Europe in 1927, and began working for a magazine called Judge, the leading humor magazine in America at the time, submitting both carto</span>
  <span id="freeText15462928492295742856" style="display:none">Theodor Seuss Geisel was born 2 March 1904 in Springfield, MA. He graduated Dartmouth College in 1925, and proceeded on to Oxford University with the intent of acquiring a doctorate in literature. At Oxford he met Helen Palmer, who he wed in 1927. He returned from Europe in 1927, and began working for a magazine called Judge, the leading humor magazine in America at the time, submitting both cartoons and humorous articles for them. Additionally, he was submitting cartoons to Life, Vanity Fair and Liberty. In some of his works, he'd made reference to an insecticide called Flit. These references gained notice, and led to a contract to draw comic ads for Flit. This association lasted 17 years, gained him national exposure, and coined the catchphrase "Quick, Henry, the Flit!" <br /><br />In 1936 on the way to a vaction in Europe, listening to the rhythm of the ship's engines, he came up with And to Think That I Saw It on Mulberry Street, which was then promptly rejected by the first 43 publishers he showed it to. Eventually in 1937 a friend published the book for him, and it went on to at least moderate success. <br /><br />During WW II, Geisel joined the army and was sent to Hollywood. Captain Geisel would write for Frank Capra's Signal Corps Unit (for which he won the Legion of Merit) and do documentaries (he won Oscar's for Hitler Lives and Design for Death). He also created a cartoon called Gerald McBoing-Boing which also won him an Oscar. <br /><br />In May of 1954, Life published a report concerning illiteracy among school children. The report said, among other things, that children were having trouble to read because their books were boring. This inspired Geisel's publisher, and prompted him to send Geisel a list of 400 words he felt were important, asked him to cut the list to 250 words (the publishers idea of how many words at one time a first grader could absorb), and write a book. Nine months later, Geisel, using 220 of the words given to him published The Cat in the Hat, which went on to instant success. <br /><br />In 1960 Bennett Cerf bet Geisel $50 that he couldn't write an entire book using only fifty words. The result was Green Eggs and Ham. Cerf never paid the $50 from the bet. <br /><br />Helen Palmer Geisel died in 1967. Theodor Geisel married Audrey Stone Diamond in 1968. Theodor Seuss Geisel died 24 September 1991. <br /><br />Also worked under the pen name:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/398177.Theo_Le_Sieg" rel="nofollow noopener">Theo Le Sieg</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15462928492295742856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
